Two Interpretations of the Hadith of God's Coming
Two exegetical aspects for the hadith of God coming in different forms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two interpretive approaches that safeguard divine transcendence when explaining the hadith of God coming in different images.

Core Idea
God's coming in images is interpreted as coming with an angel or as manifesting attributes.

The hadith about God appearing to believers in different forms can be troubling if taken literally. Imam Razi offers two scholarly interpretations that preserve divine transcendence while accepting the hadith's authenticity. These interpretations show how classical theologians reconciled scriptural reports with rational principles.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its context
Begin by reading the full hadith as narrated by Abu Hurayra. Notice that the believers first see God in an unrecognized form and later in a familiar one.
The hadith is about the final trial before entering Paradise.
2
Understand the first interpretation
The first aspect takes the preposition 'in' to mean 'with'. Thus God comes 'with' an image, not 'in' it. That image is an angel acting as a test. Recognize the support from Ibn Abbas's commentary on Quran 2:210.
This interpretation preserves God's transcendence by distinguishing His essence from the form shown.
3
Explore the second interpretation
The second interpretation redefines 'image' (صورة) as 'attribute' (صفة). God manifests attributes like might in a way believers have not experienced before.
This resolves the apparent change by referring to attributes, not essence.
4
Reflect on the purpose
Both interpretations aim to affirm the hadith's eschatological reality while avoiding anthropomorphism. Consider why such careful exegesis is necessary in Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخبر الثالث : ما روى صاحب شرح السنة ، - رحمه الله - في في كتابه ، في باب و آخر من يخرج من الغار ، عن أبى هريرة ( رضى الله عنه ) في حديث طويل ، عن رسول الله له أنه قال : « فيأتيهم الله في غير الصورة التي يعرفون . فيقول : أنا ربكم . فيقولون : نعوذ بالله . هذا مكاننا ، حتى يأتينا ربنا ، فإن بيننا وبينه علامة . فإذا أتانا ربنا عرفناه . فيأتيهم الله فى الصورة التى يعرفون . فيقولون : أنت ربنا، فيتبعونه ،

واعلم : أن الكلام على هذا الحديث من وجهين :

الأول : أن تكون « فى ، بمعنى الباء . والتقدير : فيأتيهم الله بصورة غير الصورة التي عرفوه بها في الدنيا . وذلك بأن يربهم ملكا من الملائكة . ونظيره : قول ابن عباس رضى الله عنه في قوله تعالى : « هل ينظرون إلا أن يأتيهم الله في ظلل من الغمام ، أي بظلل من الغمام . ثم إن تلك الصورة تقول : أنا ربكم . وكأن ذلك آخر محنة تقع للمكلفين في دار الآخرة ، وتكون الفائدة فيه : تثبيت المؤمنين على القول الصالح : وإنما يقال : الدنيا دار محنة ، والآخرة دار الجزاء : على الأعم والأغلب ، وإن كان يقع في كل واحدة منهما ما يقع في الأخرى نادرا

أما قوله عليه السلام : « إنهم يقولون : إذا جاء ربنا عرفناه ، فيحمل على أن يكون المراد : فإذا جاء إحسان ربنا ، عرفناه . وقوله : « فيأتيهم الله في الصورة التي يعرفونها ، فمعناه : يأتيهم بالصورة التي يعرفون أنها من أمارات الإحسان .

وأما قوله عليه السلام : « فيقولون : بيننا وبينه علامة ، فيحتمل أن تكون تلك العلامة : كونه تعالى في حقيقته مخالفا للجواهر و الأعراض. فإذا رأوا تلك الحقيقة عرفوا أنه هو الله ..

التأويل الثاني : أن يكون المراد من الصورة : الصفة . والمعنى : أن يظهر لهم من بطش الله وشدة بأسه ، ما لم يأله وه ولم يعتادوه من معاملة
The third report: What the author of Sharh al-Sunnah, may Allah have mercy on him, narrated in his book, in the chapter 'The Last to Emerge from the Cave' from Abu Hurayrah, may Allah be pleased with him, in a long hadith from the Messenger of Allah that he said: 'So Allah comes to them in an image other than that which they know, and says: "I am your Lord." They say: "We seek refuge in Allah. This is our place until our Lord comes to us. Indeed, between us and Him is a sign. So when our Lord comes to us, we will recognize Him." So Allah comes to them in the image which they know, and they say: "You are our Lord," and they follow Him.' Know that the discussion on this hadith has two aspects: First: That 'in' (في) means 'with' (ب). So the meaning: Allah comes to them with an image other than the image by which they knew Him in the world. That is by showing them an angel from the angels. Its parallel: The saying of Ibn 'Abbas, may Allah be pleased with him, regarding His statement: 'Do they wait except that Allah should come to them in canopies of clouds' (Qur'an 2:210), meaning with canopies of clouds. Then that image says: 'I am your Lord.' And perhaps that is the last trial that befalls the responsible individuals in the abode of the Hereafter, and the benefit in it is to confirm the believers upon the righteous saying. Indeed, it is said: The world is the abode of trial, and the Hereafter is the abode of recompense, in the most general and predominant sense, although each one may rarely contain what occurs in the other. As for his statement, peace be upon him: 'They say: When our Lord comes, we recognize Him' – it is interpreted that what is meant is: when the goodness of our Lord comes, we recognize Him. And his statement: 'So Allah comes to them in the image which they know' – its meaning: He comes to them with the image which they know to be among the signs of goodness. As for his statement, peace be upon him: 'Between us and Him is a sign' – it is possible that that sign is that the Exalted One in His essence is different from atoms and accidents. So when they see that essence, they know that He is Allah. The second interpretation: That what is meant by 'image' is the attribute. The meaning: He manifests to them from the might of Allah and the severity of His force that which they had not seen nor been accustomed to from His treatment.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage presents a third hadith from the author of Sharh al-Sunnah (likely al-Baghawi) about God appearing to people in different forms on the Day of Judgment. The hadith describes believers recognizing God by a sign. The author then provides two aspects of interpretation. The first aspect is linguistic: the preposition 'in' (في) is taken to mean 'with' (باء), so the meaning is that God comes 'with' an image, not 'in' an image. This is supported by Ibn Abbas's interpretation of a Qur'anic verse. The image is then identified as an angel acting as a test for believers. The author then explains that the recognition of God refers to recognition of His goodness, and the sign between them is God's essential difference from created things (transcendence). The second interpretation takes 'image' to mean 'attribute', so the coming of God in different images refers to the manifestation of His attributes, such as His might, in ways the believers had not experienced before. Both interpretations safeguard divine transcendence while affirming the hadith's eschatological reality.

Key Terms
الصورة
الصفة
المحنة
الإحسان
الجواهر والأعراض
بطش

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith implies God physically changes form.
Correction: The two interpretations show that the 'different images' refer either to an angel acting as a test or to manifestations of attributes, not a change in God's essence.

Checkpoint
In the first aspect of interpreting the hadith about God coming in different images, what does the preposition 'في' (in) mean?
A) It means 'in' literally.
B) It means 'with'.
C) It means 'from'.
D) It means 'upon'.

Key Takeaway
The two aspects of interpretation show that the hadith's apparent anthropomorphism is resolved through linguistic or attribute-based exegesis, preserving divine transcendence.

?

Two Interpretations of the Hadith of Allah's Coming
Imam Razi explains two interpretations of a hadith about Allah's coming in a form.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two linguistic interpretations of the hadith about Allah's coming that safeguard divine transcendence.

Core Idea
The hadith about Allah's coming is interpreted figuratively to preserve His transcendence.

Imam Razi tackles a challenging hadith that might suggest Allah appears in a physical form. He offers two sophisticated linguistic interpretations: one reinterpreting the preposition 'in' as 'with', and the other understanding 'form' as 'attribute'. These interpretations ensure that the text is understood in a way consistent with Allah's absolute incomparability (tanzih). In this lesson, we will explore these two interpretations and see how they uphold tanzih.

Guided Path
1
Understand the problem
The hadith appears to describe Allah coming in a form. Recognize why this is problematic for divine transcendence and how Imam Razi approaches the issue.
The problem stems from literal reading; Razi offers alternative readings.
2
First interpretation: 'in' as 'with'
Examine the reinterpretation of the particle 'في' as 'باء', making the phrase 'with a form' rather than 'in a form'. Understand that the form is an angel, and see the support from Ibn Abbas.
This interpretation avoids attributing a form to Allah directly.
3
Second interpretation: 'form' as 'attribute'
Explore the alternative where 'صورة' means 'صفة' (attribute), shifting the meaning to manifestations of divine attributes—first severity, then mercy.
This interpretation also preserves transcendence by not attributing a literal form.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم : أن الكلام على هذا الحديث من وجهين :
الأول : أن تكون « فى ، بمعنى الباء . والتقدير : فيأتيهم الله بصورة غير الصورة التي عرفوه بها في الدنيا . وذلك بأن يربهم ملكا من الملائكة . ونظيره : قول ابن عباس رضى الله عنه في قوله تعالى : « هل ينظرون إلا أن يأتيهم الله في ظلل من الغمام ، أي بظلل من الغمام . ثم إن تلك الصورة تقول : أنا ربكم . وكأن ذلك آخر محنة تقع للمكلفين في دار الآخرة ، وتكون الفائدة فيه : تثبيت المؤمنين على القول الصالح : وإنما يقال : الدنيا دار محنة ، والآخرة دار الجزاء : على الأعم والأغلب ، وإن كان يقع في كل واحدة منهما ما يقع في الأخرى نادرا
•
أما قوله عليه السلام : « إنهم يقولون : إذا جاء ربنا عرفناه ، فيحمل على أن يكون المراد : فإذا جاء إحسان ربنا ، عرفناه . وقوله : « فيأتيهم الله في الصورة التي يعرفونها ، فمعناه : يأتيهم بالصورة التي يعرفون أنها من أمارات الإحسان .
وأما قوله عليه السلام : « ( فيقولون ) : بيننا وبينه علامة ، فيحتمل أن تكون تلك العلامة : كونه تعالى في حقيقته مخالفا للجواهر و الأعراض. فإذا رأوا تلك الحقيقة عرفوا أنه هو الله ..
التأويل الثاني : أن يكون المراد من الصورة : الصفة . والمعنى : أن يظهر لهم من بطش الله وشدة بأسه ، ما لم يألهوه ولم يعتادوه من معاملة الله تعالى معهم . ثم تأتيهم بعد ذلك أنواع الرحمة والكرامة ، على الوجه الذي اعتادوه وألفروه .
Know that the discussion on this hadith is from two aspects: The first: that 'in' is in the meaning of 'with'. And the estimation: Allah will come to them with a form other than the form in which they knew Him in the world. That is by showing them a king from the angels. And its parallel is the saying of Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with him, regarding His statement, the Exalted: 'Do they wait except that Allah should come to them in canopies of clouds' meaning with canopies of clouds. Then that form says: I am your Lord. And it is as if that is the last trial that occurs to the obligated ones in the abode of the Hereafter, and the benefit in it is: strengthening the believers upon the correct statement. And indeed it is said: the world is the abode of trial, and the Hereafter is the abode of recompense: generally and predominantly, although in each of them something that occurs in the other may rarely happen. As for his statement, peace be upon him: 'Indeed they say: when our Lord comes we will recognize Him', it is interpreted to mean: when the goodness of our Lord comes, we will recognize Him. And his statement: 'And Allah will come to them in the form they know', its meaning is: He will come to them with the form that they know is from the signs of goodness. And as for his statement, peace be upon him: 'They say: between us and Him is a sign', it is possible that that sign is: that He, the Exalted, in His essence is different from substances and accidents. So when they see that essence, they will know that He is Allah. The second interpretation: that the intended meaning of 'form' is attribute. And the meaning: that there will appear to them from the might of Allah and the severity of His punishment, which they had not known and were not accustomed to in the treatment of Allah, the Exalted, with them. Then thereafter types of mercy and generosity will come to them in the manner that they had become accustomed to and familiar with.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of two interpretations of a hadith about Allah coming to the believers in a form on the Day of Resurrection. The author, Imam Razi, begins by stating that the discussion has two aspects. The first interpretation focuses on the particle 'في' (in), arguing that it carries the meaning of 'with' (باء). Thus the hadith means Allah will come with a form, i.e., accompanied by a form, not that He Himself assumes a form. The form is an angel, and the author supports this with Ibn Abbas's interpretation of a Quranic verse. The author then elaborates on the purpose of this trial: to test the believers and strengthen them. The second interpretation shifts to the word 'form' (صورة), interpreting it as 'attribute' (صفة). Here, the meaning is that Allah will first manifest His severity and power in an unfamiliar way, then afterward mercy in a familiar way. This avoids any literal attribution of a physical form to Allah. Throughout, the author maintains a careful linguistic analysis to uphold divine transcendence.

الصورة
الصفة
المحنة

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith means Allah will literally appear in a physical, corporeal form on the Day of Judgment.
Correction: Imam Razi shows the hadith must be interpreted figuratively: either 'in' means 'with' (so Allah comes with a form, i.e., an angel), or 'form' means 'attribute' (so the coming refers to manifestation of divine attributes, not a physical form). Both interpretations preserve Allah's transcendence and incomparability.

Key Takeaway
Imam Razi's two linguistic interpretations protect divine transcendence by reinterpreting key terms in the hadith.

Interpreting the Hadith 'I Saw My Lord in the Best Form'
Imam Razi interprets a hadith to negate anthropomorphism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi interprets the hadith 'I saw my Lord in the best form' in a way that avoids attributing a form to Allah, maintaining divine transcendence.

Core Idea
The phrase 'in the best form' describes the Prophet, not Allah.

One of the most subtle hadiths about the vision of Allah is the Prophet's statement 'I saw my Lord in the best form.' Some might take this literally, but Imam Razi shows that the Arabic grammar and context point to a different meaning. In this lesson, we will follow his careful analysis: first, he determines whether the description belongs to the seer or the seen, then he unpacks the two possible meanings of 'form.'

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the original Arabic of Imam Razi's text once. Notice how he breaks down the hadith into grammatical possibilities.
Focus on the key terms: صفات الراني and صفات المرئى.
2
Understand the two attributions
Identify Imam Razi's first move: the phrase 'in the best form' could describe the seer (Prophet) or the seen (Allah). He gives a linguistic analogy to clarify.
The analogy: 'I entered upon the amir in the best state' describes the speaker's state, not the amir's.
3
Explore the two interpretations of 'form'
Once the phrase is attributed to the seer, Imam Razi presents two meanings of 'form': the literal physical form and the attribute (spiritual state). Work through each meaning.
The first interpretation refers to the Prophet's physical beautification; the second to his spiritual honor.
4
Reflect on the theological motive
Consider why Imam Razi goes through this effort: to protect Allah from being described with a form or attribute that implies likeness to creation.
This is a classic kalam approach to ambiguous hadiths.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخير الرابع : ما روى عنه عليه السلام أنه قال : رأيت ربي في أحسن صورة ، واعلم : أن قوله عليه السلام : في أحسن صورة يحتمل أن يكون من صفات الراني. كما يقال : دخلت على الأمير على أحسن هيئة . أي : وانا كنت على أحسن هيئة ، ويحتمل أن يكون ذلك من صفات المرئى .
فإن كان ذلك من صفات الرائى . كان قوله : « على أحسن صورة ، عائدا إلى الرسول وفيه وجهان :
الأول : أن يكون المراد من الصورة : نفس الصورة . فيكون المعنى : أن الله تعالى زين خلقه وجمل صورته عندما رأى ربه . وذلك يكون سبباً لمزيد الإكرام في حق الرسول عليه السلام .
الثاني : أن يكون المراد من الصورة : الصفة . ويكون المعنى : الإخبار عن حسن حاله عند الله ، وأنه أنعم عليه بوجوه عظيمة من الإنعام كما كان . وذلك لأن الرائى قد يكون بحيث يتلقاه المرئى بالإكرام والتعظيم ، وقد يكون بخلافه فعرفنا الرسول عليه السلام أن حالته كانت من القسم الأول .
The fourth point: what was narrated from him, may peace be upon him, that he said: 'I saw my Lord in the best form.' And know that his statement, peace be upon him: 'in the best form' is likely to be from the attributes of the seer. As it is said: I entered upon the amir in the best state, i.e., I was in the best state. And it is likely that it is from the attributes of the seen. If it is from the attributes of the seer, then his statement 'in the best form' refers to the Messenger, and it has two aspects: The first: that the intended meaning of 'form' is the form itself. So the meaning is: Allah the Exalted beautified his creation and adorned his form when he saw his Lord. And that would be a cause for additional honor for the Messenger, peace be upon him. The second: that the intended meaning of 'form' is attribute. And the meaning is: informing about his good state with Allah, and that He has bestowed upon him great types of favor as was. And that is because the seer may be such that the seen receives him with honor and veneration, or contrary. So the Messenger, peace be upon him, informed us that his state was of the first category.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage is an interpretation of the hadith 'I saw my Lord in the best form' narrated from the Prophet. Imam Razi states that the phrase 'in the best form' could be an attribute of the seer (the Prophet) or of the seen (Allah). He provides a linguistic analogy: saying 'I entered upon the amir in the best state' describes the state of the person entering, not the amir. If it applies to the seer, then it has two possible meanings. First, 'form' literally means physical form, and Allah beautified the Prophet's appearance when he saw Him, as an honor. Second, 'form' means attribute (صفة), so the phrase indicates the Prophet's excellent spiritual state with Allah, like being received with honor. The author thus avoids any suggestion that Allah has a form. The explanation is methodical: first determining whether the description belongs to the seer or the seen, then further distinguishing between literal and metaphorical meanings of 'form'.

Key Terms
أحسن صورة
صفات الراني
صفات المرئى
الصورة
الصفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith 'I saw my Lord in the best form' means that Allah has a physical form or shape.
Correction: Imam Razi demonstrates that the phrase 'in the best form' is more plausibly attributed to the seer (the Prophet), not to Allah. He offers two interpretations that avoid ascribing any form to Allah, preserving divine transcendence.

Checkpoint

A) Form as physical shape and form as attribute
B) Form as light and form as darkness
C) Form as angel and form as human
D) Form as mercy and form as punishment

Key Takeaway
Imam Razi interprets the hadith 'I saw my Lord in the best form' as referring to the Prophet's honor or physical beautification, not to Allah having a form.

The Two Possibilities in the Hadith of Seeing Allah
Razi introduces the hadith and presents the two possibilities for the phrase's attribution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the phrase 'in a beautiful form' can be interpreted as an attribute of the Prophet or an attribute of what he saw, and why this distinction is critical for maintaining divine transcendence.

Core Idea
The hadith's description is about the seer or the seen, not Allah's essence.

Imam Razi opens his interpretation by highlighting the grammatical ambiguity in the Prophet's saying. The phrase 'in a beautiful form' could describe the state of the Prophet or the appearance of what he saw. This initial distinction is crucial because it steers the understanding away from any literal attribution of physical form to Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic phrase and translation
Read the opening words of the hadith and Razi's initial comment. Notice the grammatical ambiguity he highlights.
The phrase 'in a beautiful form' is a prepositional phrase that could attach to either the subject or the object.
2
Identify the two possible referents
Razi explicitly states that the phrase could be an attribute of the seer (the Prophet) or an attribute of the seen (what he saw, i.e., Allah). Write down these two possibilities.
He provides an analogy from everyday speech: 'I entered upon the emir in a beautiful state' can describe the speaker, not the emir.
3
Reflect on the purpose of this ambiguity
Consider why Razi starts with a grammatical point. How does this help protect the doctrine of tanzih (divine transcendence)?
By showing that the phrase can be read as describing the Prophet, Razi immediately rules out a literal interpretation of Allah having a form.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخير الرابع : ما روى عنه عليه السلام أنه قال : رأيت ربى في : أحسن صورة ، واعلم : أن قوله ( عليه السلام ) : فى أحسن صورة يحتمل أن يكون من صفات الراني. كما يقال : دخلت على الأمير على أحسن هيئة . أى : وانا كنت على أحسن هيئة ، ويحتمل أن يكون ذلك من صفات المرئى . فإن كان ذلك من صفات الرائى . كان قوله : « على أحسن صورة ، عائدا إلى ( الرسول ) وفيه و جهان : الأول : أن يكون المراد من الصورة : نفس الصورة . فيكون المعنى : أن الله تعالى زين خلقه وجمل صورته عندما رأى ربه . وذلك يكون سبباً لمزيد الإكرام في حق الرسول عليه السلام . الثاني : أن يكون المراد من الصورة : الصفة . ويكون المعنى : الإخبار عن حسن حاله عند الله ، وأنه أنعم عليه بوجوه عظيمة من الإنعام ( كما كان ) وذلك لأن الرائى قد يكون بحيث يتلقاه المرئى بالإكرام والتعظيم ، وقد يكون بخلافه فعرفنا الرسول عليه السلام أن ( حالته كانت ) من القسم الأول . و أما إن كان عائدا إلى المربى . ففيه وجوه : الأول : أن يكون عليه السلام رأى ربه في المنام، في صورة مخصوصة وذلك جائز ، لأن الرؤيا من تصرفات الخيال ، ولا ينفك ذلك عن صورة متخيلة . الثاني : أن يكون المراد من الصورة : الصفة . وذلك لأنه تعالى لماخص بمزيد الإكرام والإنعام في الوقت الذي رآه . صح أن يقال في العرف المعتاد - : إنى رأيته على أحسن صورة، وأجمل هيئة . الثالث : لعله عليه السلام لما رآه ، اطلع على نوع من صفات الجلال والعزة والعظمة ، ما كان مطلعاً عليه قبل ذلك .
The fourth report: What was narrated from him (peace be upon him) that he said: 'I saw my Lord in a beautiful form.' Know that his saying (peace be upon him) 'in a beautiful form' could be an attribute of the seer, just as it is said: 'I entered upon the emir in a beautiful state,' meaning I was in a beautiful state. And it could be an attribute of the seen. If it is an attribute of the seer, then his saying 'in a beautiful form' refers back to the Messenger (peace be upon him), and there are two aspects: First: that by form is meant the form itself; the meaning is that Allah adorned his creation and beautified his form when he saw his Lord, and that is a cause for additional honor for the Messenger. Second: that by form is meant the attribute; the meaning is informing about his good state with Allah, and that He bestowed upon him great types of favor. This is because the seer may be such that the seen treats him with honor and veneration, or the opposite, so we know that the Messenger's state was of the first kind. And if it refers to the seen, then there are aspects: First: that he (peace be upon him) saw his Lord in a dream in a specific form; that is permissible because visions are from the operations of imagination and cannot be free from an imagined form. Second: that by form is meant the attribute; because Allah distinguished him with additional honor and favor at the time he saw Him, it is correct in customary usage to say: 'I saw him in the best form and most beautiful appearance.' Third: perhaps when he saw Him, he came to know a type of the attributes of majesty, might, and greatness that he had not known before.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage interprets the fourth hadith where the Prophet says 'I saw my Lord in a beautiful form.' Imam Razi begins by noting that the phrase 'in a beautiful form' could be an attribute of the seer (the Prophet) or of the seen (Allah). He first explains the possibility that it refers to the seer, giving two interpretations: either the Prophet's physical form was beautified at that moment as an honor from Allah, or the phrase describes the Prophet's excellent state and the great favors bestowed upon him. Then he explains the possibility that it refers to the seen, giving three interpretations: the first is that it was a dream vision with a specific form, which is permissible because dreams involve imagination. The second is that the phrase refers to Allah's attributes of honor and favor manifested at that time, and in customary language one can say 'I saw him in the best form' meaning in a state of great generosity. The third is that the Prophet gained new knowledge of Allah's majestic attributes that he did not have before. Thus, Razi consistently defends divine transcendence by interpreting 'form' metaphorically or contextually, avoiding any literal attribution of physical form to Allah.

صورة
رؤية
صفات الرائى
صفات المرئى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith proves Allah has a physical form.
Correction: Razi shows the phrase can grammatically describe the seer's state, not the seen.

Checkpoint

A) The seer (Prophet) or the seen (Allah)
B) The Prophet's physical body or the angels
C) The dream or the imagination
D) The form or the attribute

Key Takeaway
The phrase 'in a beautiful form' is ambiguous and can be understood as describing the Prophet's state rather than Allah's appearance.

?

When the Phrase Describes the Seer – Two Aspects
Razi explains the two interpretations when the phrase is attributed to the seer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two interpretations Razi offers if the phrase 'in a beautiful form' describes the Prophet, and how each safeguards divine transcendence.

Core Idea
The Prophet's 'beautiful form' means either physical beautification or metaphorical honor.

Having established that the phrase could describe the seer, Razi now explores this path more deeply. He offers two interpretations: one where the Prophet's actual form was made beautiful by Allah as a sign of honor, and another where the phrase metaphorically describes the Prophet's excellent state and the great favors he received at that moment.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the section where Razi explains the two aspects under the assumption the phrase describes the seer.
The passage uses the terms 'نفس الصورة' (the form itself) and 'الصفة' (the attribute).
2
Distinguish the two interpretations
The first interpretation takes 'form' literally: Allah beautified the Prophet's physical form. The second takes 'form' metaphorically to mean 'attribute' or 'quality,' i.e., the Prophet's state of honor.
Notice how both interpretations avoid attributing any form to Allah.
3
Reflect on the underlying purpose
Both interpretations serve to honor the Prophet. The first is a physical honor, the second a spiritual one. Consider why Razi includes both.
This shows the flexibility of interpretation while maintaining theological correctness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخير الرابع : ما روى عنه عليه السلام أنه قال : رأيت ربى في : أحسن صورة ، واعلم : أن قوله ( عليه السلام ) : فى أحسن صورة يحتمل أن يكون من صفات الراني. كما يقال : دخلت على الأمير على أحسن هيئة . أى : وانا كنت على أحسن هيئة ، ويحتمل أن يكون ذلك من صفات المرئى . فإن كان ذلك من صفات الرائى . كان قوله : « على أحسن صورة ، عائدا إلى ( الرسول ) وفيه و جهان : الأول : أن يكون المراد من الصورة : نفس الصورة . فيكون المعنى : أن الله تعالى زين خلقه وجمل صورته عندما رأى ربه . وذلك يكون سبباً لمزيد الإكرام في حق الرسول عليه السلام . الثاني : أن يكون المراد من الصورة : الصفة . ويكون المعنى : الإخبار عن حسن حاله عند الله ، وأنه أنعم عليه بوجوه عظيمة من الإنعام ( كما كان ) وذلك لأن الرائى قد يكون بحيث يتلقاه المرئى بالإكرام والتعظيم ، وقد يكون بخلافه فعرفنا الرسول عليه السلام أن ( حالته كانت ) من القسم الأول . و أما إن كان عائدا إلى المربى . ففيه وجوه : الأول : أن يكون عليه السلام رأى ربه في المنام، في صورة مخصوصة وذلك جائز ، لأن الرؤيا من تصرفات الخيال ، ولا ينفك ذلك عن صورة متخيلة . الثاني : أن يكون المراد من الصورة : الصفة . وذلك لأنه تعالى لماخص بمزيد الإكرام والإنعام في الوقت الذي رآه . صح أن يقال في العرف المعتاد - : إنى رأيته على أحسن صورة، وأجمل هيئة . الثالث : لعله عليه السلام لما رآه ، اطلع على نوع من صفات الجلال والعزة والعظمة ، ما كان مطلعاً عليه قبل ذلك .
The fourth report: What was narrated from him (peace be upon him) that he said: 'I saw my Lord in a beautiful form.' Know that his saying (peace be upon him) 'in a beautiful form' could be an attribute of the seer, just as it is said: 'I entered upon the emir in a beautiful state,' meaning I was in a beautiful state. And it could be an attribute of the seen. If it is an attribute of the seer, then his saying 'in a beautiful form' refers back to the Messenger (peace be upon him), and there are two aspects: First: that by form is meant the form itself; the meaning is that Allah adorned his creation and beautified his form when he saw his Lord, and that is a cause for additional honor for the Messenger. Second: that by form is meant the attribute; the meaning is informing about his good state with Allah, and that He bestowed upon him great types of favor. This is because the seer may be such that the seen treats him with honor and veneration, or the opposite, so we know that the Messenger's state was of the first kind. And if it refers to the seen, then there are aspects: First: that he (peace be upon him) saw his Lord in a dream in a specific form; that is permissible because visions are from the operations of imagination and cannot be free from an imagined form. Second: that by form is meant the attribute; because Allah distinguished him with additional honor and favor at the time he saw Him, it is correct in customary usage to say: 'I saw him in the best form and most beautiful appearance.' Third: perhaps when he saw Him, he came to know a type of the attributes of majesty, might, and greatness that he had not known before.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage interprets the fourth hadith where the Prophet says 'I saw my Lord in a beautiful form.' Imam Razi begins by noting that the phrase 'in a beautiful form' could be an attribute of the seer (the Prophet) or of the seen (Allah). He first explains the possibility that it refers to the seer, giving two interpretations: either the Prophet's physical form was beautified at that moment as an honor from Allah, or the phrase describes the Prophet's excellent state and the great favors bestowed upon him. Then he explains the possibility that it refers to the seen, giving three interpretations: the first is that it was a dream vision with a specific form, which is permissible because dreams involve imagination. The second is that the phrase refers to Allah's attributes of honor and favor manifested at that time, and in customary language one can say 'I saw him in the best form' meaning in a state of great generosity. The third is that the Prophet gained new knowledge of Allah's majestic attributes that he did not have before. Thus, Razi consistently defends divine transcendence by interpreting 'form' metaphorically or contextually, avoiding any literal attribution of physical form to Allah.

Key Terms
صورة
صفة
صفات الرائى

A) The form itself (physical beautification)
B) The attribute of honor
C) A dream image
D) The form of Allah

Key Takeaway
The two interpretations show Razi's commitment to both respecting the text and safeguarding divine transcendence by explaining the phrase as describing the Prophet's honor.

What would need to change in your heart and actions for you to truly feel that your state is one that deserves divine honor?
?
Razi explains that the Prophet's form was beautified as a sign of honor. Are you content with your own form and state before Allah, or do you see areas where you need to beautify your character and obedience to become worthy of His nearness? ?
The two interpretations both lead to the conclusion that the Prophet was treated with great respect. How does knowing that even the Prophet's physical appearance was honored by Allah impact your view of your own body and the way you present yourself to your Creator? Will you now treat your body as a gift to be beautified through worship and gratitude?

When the Phrase Describes the Seen – Three Aspects
Razi presents three interpretations when the phrase refers to the seen.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three interpretations Razi offers if the phrase 'in a beautiful form' describes what the Prophet saw (Allah), and how each avoids attributing a physical form to Allah.

Core Idea
The seen's 'beautiful form' can be a dream, a metaphor, or new knowledge, never a physical form.

After exploring the seer interpretation, Razi turns to the possibility that the phrase describes what was seen. He provides three distinct interpretations: the first is that it was a dream vision with a specific, permissible form; the second is that 'form' means attribute, so Allah's generous treatment is described as a beautiful form; the third is that the Prophet gained new knowledge of Allah's majestic attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the section where Razi lists three interpretations under the assumption the phrase describes the seen.
Note the numbering: الأول, الثاني, الثالث.
2
Understand each interpretation
First: dream vision with an imagined form. Second: metaphorical attribute referring to Allah's honor and favor. Third: new knowledge of Allah's attributes of majesty.
All three avoid saying Allah has a physical form.
3
Compare the three
Notice that the first is a literal dream, the second is metaphorical, and the third is epistemological. Each offers a different way to understand the hadith without violating tanzih.
This shows Razi's comprehensive approach to prophetic reports.

Three Interpretations of a Prophetic Vision
Imam Razi enumerates three interpretations of a prophetic report.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three interpretations of the phrase 'I saw my Lord in the most beautiful form' and how they safeguard divine transcendence.

Core Idea
The 'form' in the hadith is not literal; it is either a dream, an attribute, or a glimpse of majesty.

Imam Razi presents three ways to understand the famous report where the Prophet said he saw his Lord in the most beautiful form. These interpretations protect Allah's transcendence by avoiding any physical form. Let's explore each one.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation. Notice the three numbered interpretations.
The author uses 'الأول', 'الثاني', 'الثالث' to enumerate.
2
Understand the first interpretation (dream)
The first interpretation says it was a dream, and the form is a product of imagination. This is permissible and does not imply a physical body.
Dream visions are common in prophetic tradition.
3
Understand the second interpretation (attribute)
The second interprets 'form' as 'attribute' (صفة). The phrase then means the Prophet saw his Lord with abundant honor and grace.
This is a linguistic shift from literal form to attribute.
4
Understand the third interpretation (majesty)
The third suggests the Prophet witnessed a type of divine majesty and greatness not previously known.
5
Reflect on the common theme
All three interpretations avoid literalism. They show that the hadith does not imply Allah has a physical form.
This is the key lesson for divine transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما إن كان عائدا إلى المربى. ففيه وجوه:
الأول: أن يكون عليه السلام رأى ربه في المنام، في صورة مخصوصة وذلك جائز، لأن الرؤيا من تصرفات الخيال، ولا ينفك ذلك عن صورة متخيلة.
الثاني: أن يكون المراد من الصورة: الصفة. وذلك لأنه تعالى لما خص بمزيد الإكرام والإنعام في الوقت الذي رآه، صح أن يقال في العرف المعتاد: إني رأيته على أحسن صورة، وأجمل هيئة.
الثالث: لعله عليه السلام لما رآه، اطلع على نوع من صفات الجلال والعزة والعظمة، ما كان مطلعاً عليه قبل ذلك.
And as for if it refers to the one raised [the Prophet], then in it are aspects: First: That he, peace be upon him, saw his Lord in a dream, in a particular form, and that is permissible, because the dream-vision is among the operations of the imagination, and that is not free from an imagined form. Second: That what is meant by 'form' is attribute. That is because when He, exalted, was distinguished by additional honor and favor at the time he saw Him, it is correct to say in common usage: I saw Him in the best form and most beautiful appearance. Third: Perhaps when he saw Him, he became aware of a type of the attributes of majesty, might, and greatness that he had not been aware of before that.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage gives three possible interpretations for the word 'form' (صورة) in the report 'I saw my Lord in the most beautiful form.' The first interpretation is that it was a dream, and the form is a product of the imagination—this is permissible and does not imply a physical body. The second is that 'form' here means 'attribute' (صفة), so the phrase indicates that the Prophet saw his Lord with abundant honor and grace. The third is that the Prophet witnessed a type of divine majesty and greatness that he had not previously known. All three interpretations safeguard divine transcendence by avoiding any literal physical form.

Correction: These three interpretations show that the 'form' is either a dream-image, an attribute, or a glimpse of majesty—not a literal physical form.

Interpreting the Fifth Report: Hand, Shoulders, and Coolness
Imam Razi interprets the fifth report's phrases as metaphors.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi interprets the anthropomorphic expressions in the hadith of the Prophet's dream, using metaphorical and contextual arguments to uphold divine transcendence.

Core Idea
Anthropomorphic images in the hadith point to divine care, not a physical body.

This lesson examines the fifth report, a hadith that describes the Prophet's dream of seeing his Lord. Imam Razi provides careful interpretations of phrases like 'hand,' 'between shoulders,' and 'coolness,' showing how they must be understood metaphorically to preserve Allah's transcendence. By following his reasoning, you'll learn a key approach in Islamic theology: interpreting scriptural expressions in a way that reconciles revelation with reason.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith text and translation
Start by reading the complete Arabic hadith as narrated from Ibn Abbas, along with its literal English translation. Notice the phrases that will be interpreted: 'hand,' 'between shoulders,' 'coolness,' and the resulting knowledge.
The hadith includes a question about the highest assembly disputing, which is not the focus of interpretation here.
2
Understand the two interpretations of 'hand'
Imam Razi gives two possibilities for 'hand': (1) it is a metaphor for care and attention, as in 'so-and-so has a hand in this craft'; (2) it means 'blessing' (ni'mah), as in 'white hand.' Reflect on how both avoid a literal body part.
3
Analyze 'between shoulders' and its variant
For 'between my shoulders,' Razi says if the wording is authentic, it conveys kindness and mercy reaching the heart. He also notes a variant 'between my breasts' (كنف), meaning care and protection. See how the interpretation shifts to a spiritual meaning.
The variant 'كنف' is crucial for understanding the metaphorical intent.
4
Explore the dual meaning of 'coolness'
Razi offers two possibilities for 'I found its coolness': (1) the coolness of a blessed, comfortable life, or (2) the perfection of knowledge (ma'arif). He favors the latter because the hadith ends with the Prophet knowing what is between east and west, which requires knowledge.
This shows how context is used to prefer one interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخبر الخامس: ما روي عن ابن عباس رضي الله عنه، عن النبي أنه قال: «رأيت ربي في أحسن صورة»، قال: «فوضع يده بين كتفي، فوجدت بردها بين ثديي فعلمت ما بين السماء والأرض، ثم قال: يا محمد. قلت: لبيك وسعديك. قال: فيم يختصم الملأ الأعلى؟ فقلت: يا رب لا أدري. فقال: في أداء الكفارات، والمشي على الأقدام إلى الجماعات، وإسباغ الوضوء على الكراهات، وانتظار الصلاة بعد الصلاة».
واعلم: أن قوله: «رأيت ربي في أحسن صورة» قد تقدم تأويله. وأما قوله: «وضع يده بين كتفي» ففيه وجهان:
الأول: المراد منه المبالغة في الاهتمام بحاله، والاعتناء بشأنه. يقال: لفلان يد في هذه الصنعة، أي هو كامل فيها.
الثاني: أن يكون المراد من اليد: النعمة. يقال: لفلان يد بيضاء، ويقال: إن أيادي فلان كثيرة.
وأما قوله: «بين كتفي» فإن صح، فالمراد منه: أنه أوصل إلى قلبه من أنواع اللطف والرحمة. وقد روي «بين كنفي»، والمراد منه مثل ما يقال: أنا في كنف فلان، وفي ظل إنعامه.
وأما قوله: «فوجدت بردها» فيحتمل أن المعنى: برد النعمة وروحها وراحتها، من قولهم: عيش بارد إذا كان رغدا، ويحتمل كمال المعارف. والذي يدل على أن المراد منه كمال المعارف قوله عليه السلام في آخر الحديث: «فعلمت ما بين المشرق والمغرب»، وما ذلك إلا لأن الله تعالى أنار قلبه وشرح صدره بالمعارف. وفي بعض الروايات: «فوجدت برد أنامله»، وسيأتي الكلام فيه إن شاء الله تعالى.
The fifth report: What was narrated from Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with him, from the Prophet that he said: 'I saw my Lord in the most beautiful form.' He said: 'He placed His hand between my shoulders, and I found its coolness between my chest, and I knew what is between the heavens and the earth. Then He said: O Muhammad. I said: At Your service and Your pleasure. He said: About what do the highest assembly dispute? I said: O Lord, I do not know. He said: About performing expiations, walking on foot to congregations, completing ablution despite hardships, and waiting for prayer after prayer.'
And know that his saying 'I saw my Lord in the most beautiful form' has already been interpreted. As for his saying 'He placed His hand between my shoulders,' it has two aspects:
First: What is meant is exaggeration in caring for his condition and attending to his affair. It is said: So-and-so has a hand in this craft, i.e., he is perfect in it.
Second: That what is meant by 'hand' is blessing. It is said: So-and-so has a white hand, and it is said: The hands of so-and-so are many.
As for his saying 'between my shoulders,' if it is authentic, what is meant is that He conveyed to his heart types of kindness and mercy. And it has been narrated as 'between my breasts' (بين كنفي), and what is meant is like what is said: I am in the care of so-and-so and in the shade of his favor.
As for his saying 'I found its coolness,' it is possible that the meaning is the coolness of blessing, its spirit, and its comfort, from their saying: a cool life, if it is abundant, and it is possible [it means] the perfection of knowledge. And what indicates that what is meant is the perfection of knowledge is his saying at the end of the hadith: 'I knew what is between the east and the west,' and that is only because Allah illuminated his heart and expanded his chest with knowledge. And in some narrations: 'I found the coolness of his fingertips,' and discussion of it will come, if Allah wills.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth report (a hadith from Ibn Abbas) and provides interpretations for its various phrases. The hadith describes the Prophet's vision of his Lord in a dream, the placing of a hand between his shoulders, and the resulting knowledge. The author first notes that the interpretation of the opening phrase has already been given. Then he gives two interpretations for 'He placed His hand between my shoulders': (1) it is a metaphor for the extreme care and attention shown to the Prophet—as when one says 'so-and-so has a hand in this craft' meaning he is skilled; (2) 'hand' means 'blessing' (نعمة), so the phrase indicates abundant blessings. For 'between my shoulders,' if the wording is authentic, it means the conveyance of kindness and mercy to the heart; a variant reading 'between my breasts' (بين كنفي) is interpreted as being in His care and protection. For 'I found its coolness,' two possibilities are given: either the coolness of a blessed and comfortable life, or the perfection of knowledge. The latter is supported by the end of the hadith where the Prophet says he knew what is between the east and west, indicating that this knowledge came from Allah illuminating his heart. A variant mentions 'coolness of his fingertips,' which will be discussed later.

Key Terms
يد
كتف
كنف
برد
نعمة
معرفة
كفارة
وضوء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that the words 'hand,' 'shoulders,' and 'coolness' refer to literal physical attributes of Allah.
Correction: Imam Razi shows that these are metaphors: 'hand' means care or blessing, 'between shoulders' conveys mercy, and 'coolness' refers to knowledge or comfort—all consistent with Allah's transcendence beyond physicality.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Razi, what does the phrase 'I found its coolness' primarily indicate, based on the context of the hadith?
A) Physical coolness of a hand
B) The coolness of a blessed life
C) The perfection of knowledge
D) Both B and C, but the context supports C

Key Takeaway
Imam Razi demonstrates that anthropomorphic phrases in the hadith must be interpreted metaphorically, in line with Allah's transcendence, using linguistic and contextual clues.

Interpreting Anthropomorphic Expressions in a Prophetic Hadith
Razi explains multiple possible meanings of 'hand', 'between the shoulders', and 'coolness' in a prophetic hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi interprets anthropomorphic expressions in a prophetic hadith by offering metaphorical meanings derived from Arabic usage and context.

Core Idea
Anthropomorphic descriptions of Allah require metaphorical interpretation.

Imam Razi demonstrates the proper method of ta'wil for problematic hadith expressions. He takes a well-known hadith and shows that words like 'hand', 'between the shoulders', and 'coolness' have plausible figurative meanings that preserve divine transcendence. This lesson walks through his reasoning and the supporting linguistic evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Razi structures his commentary: first 'hand', then 'between shoulders', then 'coolness'.
Pay attention to the Arabic idioms he cites.
2
Understand the interpretations of 'hand'
Identify the two interpretations: perfection in a craft and blessing. See how he supports each with common Arabic expressions.
The phrase 'so-and-so has a hand in this craft' is an idiom.
3
Examine the phrase 'between my shoulders'
Note the interpretation as conveying kindness and mercy to the heart, and the variant reading 'between my armpits' meaning protection.
4
Analyze 'coolness' and the supporting evidence
See the two possibilities: coolness of blessing and comfort, or completeness of knowledge. Note how the end of the hadith ('I knew what is between east and west') supports the knowledge interpretation.
This shows the importance of context in ta'wil.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأول : المراد منه : المبالغة فى الاهتمام بحاله ، والاعتناء بشأنه . يقال : لفلان يد فى هذه الصنعة ، أى هو كامل فيها .
الثاني : أن يكون المراد من اليد : النعمة : يقال . لفلان يد بيضاء، ويقال : إن أيادى فلان كثيرة .
وأما قوله : « بين كتفى »، فإن صح . فالمراد منه : أنه أوصل إلى قلبه من أنواع اللطف والرحمة . وقد روى « بين كنفى »، والمراد منه : مثل ما يقال : أنا في كنف فلا ، وفى ظل إنعامه .
وأما قوله : « فوجدت بردها »، فيحتمل أن المعنى : برد النعمة وروحها وراحتها. من قولهم : عيش بارد ، إذا كان رغدا . ويحتمل كمال المعارف . و الذي يدل على أن المراد منه : عمال المعارف : قوله عليه السلام في آخر الحديث : « فعلمت ما بين المشرق والمغرب »، وما ذلك إلا لأن الله تعالى أنار قلبه وشرح صدره بالمعارف. وفى بعض الروايات : فوجدت برد أنامله ، وسيأتي الكلام فيه إن شاء الله تعالى .
First: what is intended by it is exaggeration in caring about his state and attention to his affair. It is said: so-and-so has a hand in this craft, meaning he is perfect in it. Second: that what is intended by 'hand' is blessing. It is said: so-and-so has a white hand, and it is said: indeed the hands of so-and-so are many. As for his saying 'between my shoulders', if it is authentic, then what is intended by it is that He conveyed to his heart types of kindness and mercy. And it has been narrated 'between my armpits', and what is intended by it is like what is said: I am in the protection of so-and-so and in the shade of His favor. As for his saying 'I found its coolness', it is possible that the meaning is the coolness of blessing, its spirit, and its comfort, from their saying: a cool life, if it is plentiful. And it is possible [it means] completeness of knowledge. And what indicates that what is intended by it is completeness of knowledge is his saying, peace be upon him, at the end of the hadith: 'I knew what is between the east and the west', and that is only because Allah Almighty illuminated his heart and expanded his chest with knowledge. And in some narrations: 'I found the coolness of his fingertips', and the discussion about it will come, God willing.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage explains the metaphorical interpretations of anthropomorphic expressions in a prophetic hadith. The author (Razi) first addresses the word 'hand' (يد), offering two possible meanings: firstly, it refers to perfection and skill in a craft, as in the idiom 'so-and-so has a hand in this craft'; secondly, it means blessing (نعمة), as in 'so-and-so has a white hand' or 'the hands of so-and-so are many'. Then he discusses the phrase 'between my shoulders' (بين كتفى), interpreting it as a conveyance of kindness and mercy to the heart; an alternate narration says 'between my armpits' (بين كنفى), meaning being in God's protection and shade. Finally, he interprets the word 'coolness' (بردها) from 'I found its coolness'. It could mean the coolness of blessing and comfort, as in a cool and plentiful life. Another interpretation is 'completeness of knowledge' (كمال المعارف), supported by the hadith's concluding phrase 'I knew what is between the east and the west', indicating that God illuminated his heart with knowledge. The author also notes a variant reading 'coolness of his fingertips' and promises further discussion.

Correction: The passage shows that 'hand' must be interpreted metaphorically as perfection or blessing, not literally.

Interpreting 'Person' and 'Jealousy' in a Prophetic Hadith
Razi defines the word 'person' and interprets 'jealousy' in a prophetic hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi interprets the words 'person' and 'jealousy' in a prophetic hadith to preserve divine transcendence.

Core Idea
The terms 'person' and 'jealousy' in the hadith are interpreted metaphorically to avoid anthropomorphism.

Imam Razi addresses a hadith that uses the words 'person' and 'jealousy' in relation to Allah. To safeguard Allah's transcendence, he provides careful interpretations that shift the literal meanings towards more abstract concepts. This lesson explains those interpretations.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and identify the two problematic terms
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Notice that the hadith contains two words that require interpretation: 'person' and 'jealousy'.
The hadith is not in the Quran but is from prophetic tradition.
2
Understand Razi's interpretation of 'person' as the specific essence
Razi explains that 'person' here means the specific essence (الذات المعينة) and particular reality (الحقيقة المخصوصة), not a physical body. He uses the concept of concomitants to justify this metaphorical usage.
3
Understand Razi's interpretation of 'jealousy' as deterrence
Razi interprets 'jealousy' (الغيرة) as deterrence (الزجر), explaining that jealousy is a psychological state that leads to deterrence, so the cause is used for the effect.
4
Reflect on why these interpretations are necessary
Consider why Razi feels compelled to interpret these terms. How does each interpretation protect Allah's transcendence (tanzih)?
This connects to the broader goal of avoiding anthropomorphism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثاني في لفظ الشخص
هذا اللفظ ما ورد في القرآن. لكنه روى أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «لا شخص أحب للغيرة من الله عز وجل». وفي هذا الخبر لفظان يجب تأويلهما:
الأول: الشخص. والمراد منه: الذات المعينة والحقيقة المخصوصة. لأن الجسم الذي له شخص وحجمية، يلزم أن يكون واحدا. فإطلاق اسم الشخصية على الوحدة إطلاق اسم أحد المتلازمين على الآخر.
والثاني: لفظ الغيرة. ومعناه: الزجر. لأن الغيرة حالة نفسانية مقتضية للزجر والمنع، فكنى بالسبب عن المسبب ههنا. والله أعلم.
The Second Chapter on the Word 'Person'
This word does not occur in the Quran. But it is narrated that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'None is more beloved in jealousy than Allah, Mighty and Majestic.' In this report, there are two words that must be interpreted:
First: 'person' (الشخص). What is intended by it is the specific essence (الذات المعينة) and the particular reality (الحقيقة المخصوصة). Because a body that has a person and volume necessarily is one. So applying the name of personhood (الشخصية) to unity (الوحدة) is applying the name of one of the two concomitants to the other.
Second: the word 'jealousy' (الغيرة). Its meaning is deterrence (الزجر). Because jealousy is a psychological state that necessitates deterring and preventing. So the cause was used metaphorically for the effect here. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage is a definition and interpretation of two terms in a prophetic hadith. The author (Razi) begins a new chapter on the word 'person' (الشخص). He notes that this word does not appear in the Quran but is found in a hadith: 'None is more beloved in jealousy than Allah.' The hadith contains two words requiring interpretation: 'person' and 'jealousy'. For 'person', the intended meaning is the specific essence (الذات المعينة) and the particular reality (الحقيقة المخصوصة), not a physical body with personhood and volume. Razi explains that a body with personhood and volume is necessarily one (i.e., a single entity), so applying the term 'person' to unity is a metaphorical extension: it uses the name of one of the entailments for the other. In other words, since a person is a unified entity, personhood is predicated of unity. For 'jealousy' (الغيرة), the literal meaning is deterrence (الزجر), because jealousy is a psychological state that prompts deterrence and prevention; here the cause (jealousy) is used figuratively for the effect (deterrence).

الغيرة
الذات المعينة
الزجر
المتلازمين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the word 'person' in the hadith implies that Allah has a physical body with personhood and volume.
Correction: Razi clarifies that 'person' here means the specific essence and particular reality, not a physical body. The metaphorical usage is justified by the relationship of concomitance between personhood and unity.

Checkpoint

C) The word 'person' is not interpreted

Key Takeaway
Razi interprets 'person' as specific essence and 'jealousy' as deterrence, ensuring that the hadith does not imply anthropomorphism.

The True Meaning of al-Samad
Razi defines al-Samad, rejects body-claim, gives correct meaning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Samad cannot mean a body and what it truly means as 'the One sought for needs'.

Core Idea
Al-Samad means the One to whom we turn for needs, not a solid body.

The verse 'Allahu al-Samad' has been misinterpreted by some to imply God is a body. Imam Razi refutes these claims by showing that the word's true root meaning is 'to intend' or 'to aim for', making al-Samad refer to God as the ultimate object of all needs. Let's see how he builds this argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and its literal translation. Notice the two interpretations reported and their connection to anthropomorphism.
2
Identify the false interpretations
Look for the two interpretations of al-Samad mentioned: (1) body with no cavity, and (2) smooth stone. Both are used by anthropomorphists to claim God is a body.
These interpretations are based on linguistic usage for physical objects.
3
Understand Razi's refutation
Razi gives two refutations: first, the attribute 'One' (ahad) negates being a body; second, the description 'body with no cavity' applies only to coarse bodies, which is unfitting for God.
4
Learn the correct meaning
Razi explains that 'samad' is a verbal noun meaning 'intended', so 'al-Samad' means the One intended for all needs. He cites a line of poetry as evidence.
This aligns with the verse's context in Surah al-Ikhlas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الرابع في لفظ الصمد. قال الله تعالى : { الله الصمد }. ذكر بعضهم في تفسير الصمد : أنه الجسم الذي لا جوف له . ومنه قول من يقول لسداد القارورة : العماد . وشيء محمد أي صلب، ليس فيه رخاوة . قال ابن قتيبة : دو [؟] على هذا التفسير تكون الدال مبدلة من التاء ، وقال بعضهم : الصمد : الأملس ، من الحجر الذي لا يقبل الغبار ، ولا يدخل فيه شيء ، ولا يخرج منه شيء. واحتج قوم من جهال المشبهة بهذه الآية في إثبات أنه تعالى جسم . وهذا باطل . لأنا بينا أن كونه أحدا ينافي كونه جسما ، فمقدمة هذه الآية دالة على أنه لا يمكن أن يكون المراد من الصمد : هذا المعنى ، ولأن الصمد بهذا التفسير ، صفة الأجسام الغليظة ، وتعالى الله عن ذلك. والجواب عنه من وجهين : الأول : إن الصمد فعل بمعنى مفعول ، من صمد إليه أي قصد . والمعنى : أنه المصمود إليه في الحوائج . قال الشاعر : ألا يكر الناعي حيرى بني أسد بعمر و بن مسعود وبالسيد الصمد .
Chapter Four on the word al-Samad. God Almighty said: 'God, al-Samad.' Some mentioned in the interpretation of al-Samad that it is the body which has no cavity. And from it is the saying of one who says for the stopper of the bottle: al-'imad (the support). And something 'musammad' meaning solid, without softness. Ibn Qutayba said: ... (unclear) on this interpretation, the dal is substituted from the ta. And some said: al-Samad is the smooth, from the stone that does not accept dust, nothing enters it, and nothing comes out of it. And a group of the ignorant anthropomorphists argued by this verse to affirm that He, exalted, is a body. This is false. Because we have shown that His being One negates His being a body, so the premise of this verse indicates that it is impossible that the intended meaning of al-Samad is this meaning. And because al-Samad according to this interpretation is a description of coarse bodies, and God is exalted above that. And the answer to it is from two aspects: First: that 'samad' is a verbal noun in the sense of a passive participle, from 'samada ilayhi' meaning he intended. And the meaning is: He is the one who is intended for needs. The poet said: 'Behold, the herald does not disturb the living of Banu Asad with 'Amr ibn Mas'ud and with the chief al-Samad.'
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage is a definition and refutation. Razi begins a new chapter on the word 'al-Samad' from the Quranic verse 'Allahu al-Samad'. He first reports two interpretations from earlier scholars: (1) that al-Samad means a body with no cavity, citing linguistic usages like 'imad for a bottle stopper and 'musammad' for solid; Ibn Qutayba is quoted as saying that on this interpretation the letter dal is substituted from ta. (2) that al-Samad means smooth, like a stone that repels dust and allows nothing in or out. Then Razi notes that ignorant anthropomorphists (mushabbiha) use this verse to claim that God is a body. He refutes this with two points: first, God's attribute of being 'One' (ahad) negates the possibility of being a body, and the context of the verse (which includes 'Qul huwa Allahu ahad') prevents this meaning; second, the very description of a solid body is a property of coarse physical objects, and God is far above that. Then he provides an answer from the correct interpretation: the word 'samad' is actually a verbal noun with a passive meaning, from the root 'samada' meaning to intend or aim, so 'al-Samad' means the One who is turned to for needs. He cites a poetic line as evidence. (Note: The passage mentions two aspects but only gives the first; the second is likely on the next page.)

Key Terms
الصمد
الجسم
المشبهة
أحد
مصمود إليه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That al-Samad implies God is a solid body, like a stone or a hollow object.
Correction: Al-Samad means the One who is intended for all needs, not a physical body.

Checkpoint
According to Razi, what is the correct interpretation of al-Samad that refutes anthropomorphism?
A) It means a body without a cavity.
B) It means the One who is intended for needs.
C) It means smooth stone.
D) It means a support.

Key Takeaway
Al-Samad means the One to whom all needs are directed, not a physical body.

The Second Interpretation of al-Samad: Metaphor over Literal
Razi argues for metaphorical interpretation of al-Samad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Razi argues that the term 'al-Samad' must be interpreted metaphorically when applied to God, despite its literal meaning in Arabic.

Core Idea
Literal meaning of 'al-Samad' implies corporeality, which is impossible for God.

In this passage, Razi continues his discussion of the divine attribute 'al-Samad'. He begins by accepting the literal meaning of the word in Arabic—'solid mass into which nothing enters'—but then demonstrates why this meaning cannot apply to God. By reasoning from God's necessary existence, he shows that the term must be taken metaphorically to preserve divine transcendence. This lesson walks through his logical steps.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
First, read the Arabic original and its translation. Notice how Razi concedes the literal meaning before rejecting its application to God.
Pay attention to the phrase 'إنا سلمنا' which signals a concession.
2
Understand the literal meaning of 'al-Samad'
The literal meaning is 'solid mass into which nothing enters'. Razi accepts this as the linguistic root.
This is a classic method in kalam: affirming the linguistic meaning while denying its literal application to God.
3
Follow Razi's reason for rejecting the literal application
Razi argues that the literal meaning implies a body free from division and external influence. But God is not a body; He is the Necessary Existent, not subject to increase or decrease. Therefore, the literal meaning is impossible for God.
This reasoning relies on the principle of tanzīh (divine transcendence).
4
Conclude: necessity of metaphorical interpretation
Since the literal meaning is impossible, the term must be interpreted metaphorically. Razi implies that the metaphorical meaning refers to God being the one to whom all needs are directed, as in the well-known interpretation.
Razi closes with 'وبالله التوفيق', seeking God's success.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الثانى فى الجواب : إنا سلمنا أن الصمد في أصل اللغة : المصمت الذى لا يدخل فيه شيء غيره. إلا أنا نقول : قد دللنا على أنه لا يمكن ثبوت هذا المعنى فى حق الله تعالى ، فوجب حمل هذا اللفظ على مجازه . وذلك لأن الجسم الذي يكون هذا شأنه، يكون مبرأ عن الانفصال والتباين والتأثر عن الغير . وهو - سبحانه وتعالى - واجب الوجود لذاته . وذلك يقتضى أن يكون تعالى غير قابل للزيادة والنقصان . فكان المراد من الصمد في حقه تعالى : هذا المعنى ) وبالله التوفيق (
The second aspect in the answer: We concede that al-samad in the original language is the solid [mass] into which nothing else enters. However, we say: we have demonstrated that it is impossible to establish this meaning with respect to God Almighty, so it is necessary to carry this term to its metaphorical [meaning]. That is because a body that has this characteristic is free from division, separation, and being affected by others. And He - glorified and exalted - is necessary of existence by Himself. And that requires that the Exalted be not susceptible to increase or decrease. So what is meant by al-samad with respect to Him, exalted, is this meaning. And by God is success.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage presents the second of two answers (or aspects) regarding the interpretation of the divine attribute 'al-Samad'. Razi begins by conceding the literal meaning of 'samad' in the Arabic language: it refers to something solid and compact into which nothing can enter. However, he then argues that this literal meaning cannot be attributed to God because it implies corporeality and materiality, which are impossible for the Necessary Existent. The reasoning is that a solid body would be free from division and external influence, but God is not a body at all; He is necessary of existence by Himself, which entails that He is not subject to increase or decrease. Therefore, the term 'al-Samad' when applied to God must be interpreted metaphorically (majāz) to mean something appropriate to His essence, such as the one to whom all needs are directed, as supported by the narration of Ibn Abbas earlier. Razi closes with 'And by God is success', a common formula for seeking divine assistance. This is a classic kalam method: affirming the linguistic root but denying its literal applicability to God due to tanzīh (transcendence).

Key Terms
الصمد
المصمت
مجاز
واجب الوجود لذاته

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that Razi denies the lexical meaning of 'al-Samad' entirely.
Correction: Razi explicitly concedes the lexical meaning; he only denies its literal applicability to God.

Checkpoint
Why does Razi reject the literal meaning of 'al-Samad' for God?
A) Because the word has no clear meaning in Arabic.
B) Because the literal meaning implies corporeality and composition, which are impossible for God.
C) Because the Prophet explicitly forbade using this word.
D) Because the word only applies to inanimate objects.

Key Takeaway
When applied to God, the term 'al-Samad' must be taken metaphorically to avoid implying corporeality, because God is the Necessary Existent, not a body.

Interpreting 'Meeting' in Scripture: Razi's Two Metaphorical Interpretations
Razi introduces 'al-liqa'' and gives two metaphorical interpretations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the term 'al-liqa'' (meeting) when applied to God must be interpreted metaphorically, and what the two main interpretations are according to Imam Razi.

Core Idea
God's transcendence requires metaphorical interpretation of scriptural terms like 'meeting'.

This lesson explores how the great theologian Fakhr al-Din al-Razi handles a key term that appears in the Quran and hadith: al-liqa' (meeting). Because God is beyond space and time, any term implying physical proximity must be understood in a way befitting His majesty. Razi presents two metaphorical interpretations grounded in reason.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
The passage is cut off at the end; focus on the two interpretations given.
2
Identify the scriptural evidence
Notice the three Quranic verses and the hadith that Razi cites as containing the term 'al-liqa'.
These are the starting point for the theological discussion.
3
Understand the objection
Razi reports an objection: 'meeting' is a term for bodies, like two armies meeting. Since God is not a body, how can He be 'met'?
This is the core problem that drives the need for metaphorical interpretation.
4
Examine the first interpretation
The first interpretation equates meeting with vision (ru'ya): meeting often leads to seeing, so the cause (meeting) is used for the effect (vision).
This is a common metaphorical device in Arabic rhetoric.
5
Examine the second interpretation
The second interpretation sees meeting as submission to a king's authority: when a person meets a king, they come under his rule. So meeting God means being fully under His power.
This interpretation emphasizes God's absolute sovereignty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الخامس فى لفظ اللقاء . و بهم أنا القرآن . فقد قال الله تعالى : « الذين يظنون : أنهم ملاقوا ربهم » ، وقال : « فمن كان يرجو لقاء ربه » ، وقال : « بل هم بلقاء كافرون » ، وأما الحديث فقد قال عليه السلام : « من أحب لقاء الله أحب الله لقاءه ، ومن كره لقاء الله كره الله لقاءه » . قالوا : واللقاء من صفات الأجسام . يقال : التقى الجيشان . إذا قرب أحدهما من الآخر في المكان . واعلم : أنه لما ثبت بالدليل أنه تعالى ليس بجسم ، وجب حمل هذا اللفظ على احد وجهين : أحدهما : أن من لقى إنسانا ، فقد أدركه وأبصره . فكان المراد من اللقاء : هو الرؤية . إطلاقا لاسم السبب على المسبب . والثاني : إن الرجل إذا حضر عند ملك ، ولقيه ، دخل هناك تحت حكمه وقهره ، دخولا لا حيلة له فى دفعه . فكان ذلك اللقاء سببا لظهور قدرة الملك عليه - على هذا الوجه - فلما ظهرت قدرته وقوته وقهره
The fifth chapter on the term 'al-liqa''. And [?] that the Quran. For God Almighty said: 'Those who are certain that they will meet their Lord' and said: 'So whoever hopes for the meeting of his Lord' and said: 'Nay, they are disbelievers in the meeting [of their Lord]'. As for the hadith, he (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever loves to meet God, God loves to meet him; and whoever dislikes meeting God, God dislikes meeting him.' They said: Meeting (al-liqa') is among the attributes of bodies. It is said: The two armies met, when one drew near the other in place. Know: Since it is established by proof that the Exalted is not a body, it is necessary to carry this term to one of two aspects: One of them: that whoever meets a person has perceived and seen him. So the intended meaning of 'meeting' is vision (al-ru'ya). [This is] applying the name of the cause to the effect. The second: that a man, when he attends before a king and meets him, enters under his rule and subjugation, an entry over which he has no means of repelling. So that meeting became a cause for the manifestation of the king's power over him—in this aspect—and when his power, strength, and domination became manifest...
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage begins a new chapter on the term 'al-liqa'' (meeting), which appears in the Quran and hadith. Razi first cites three Quranic verses: 'those who are certain that they will meet their Lord' (al-Baqara 2:46), 'so whoever hopes for the meeting of his Lord' (al-Kahf 18:120), and 'nay, they are disbelievers in the meeting [of their Lord]' (al-Sajda 32:10). He also cites the hadith: 'Whoever loves to meet God, God loves to meet him...' Then he reports an objection: 'meeting' is a term predicated of bodies, e.g., two armies meeting in space. Since it is already proven that God is not a body, this term must be interpreted metaphorically. He gives two possible metaphorical interpretations. The first: meeting a person often entails seeing them, so the intended meaning of 'meeting' is 'vision' (ru'ya), i.e., the vision of God in the afterlife. This is a metaphorical usage, since the cause (meeting) is used to refer to the effect (vision). The second: when a person attends before a king, he falls under the king's authority, so 'meeting' here refers to being subject to God's power and judgment. Razi begins to explain this second aspect but the passage is cut off at the end of page 129; the argument is incomplete. Nevertheless, the basic kalam method is clear: because 'meeting' implies physical proximity and spatial relationship, which cannot apply to God, it must be carried over to a non-literal meaning that is befitting of God, such as vision or submission to divine authority.

إطلاق اسم السبب على المسبب
مجاز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'meeting God' in the Quran means literal physical meeting or spatial proximity.
Correction: Razi shows that because God is not a body, the term must be interpreted metaphorically, either as vision (in the afterlife) or as submission to divine authority.

Checkpoint
According to Razi, why must the term 'al-liqa'' (meeting) be interpreted metaphorically when applied to God?
A) Because the Quran does not use the word literally.
B) Because 'meeting' implies physical proximity, which is impossible for a non-corporeal God.
C) Because the Prophet prohibited saying that God can be met.
D) Because the word only applies to inanimate objects.

Key Takeaway
Razi demonstrates that the term 'meeting' in scripture must be understood metaphorically, either as the vision of God in the afterlife or as submission to His absolute authority, in order to uphold divine transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite Qur'anic verses about 'meeting Allah,' do you instinctively imagine a spatial encounter, or do you see it as a metaphor for beholding Him in the afterlife? How does Razi's first interpretation challenge your habitual reading of these verses?
?
Razi describes meeting a king as entering under his absolute rule. In your daily life, do you truly live as though you are under God's absolute authority, or do you compartmentalize your submission? Where is the greatest gap between your verbal acknowledgment and actual surrender?
?
The hadith says: 'Whoever loves to meet God, God loves to meet him.' Examine your heart: do you genuinely long to meet your Lord, or does the thought make you uneasy? What attachments or fears prevent that yearning? What would need to change in your life for you to sincerely desire that meeting?
